                              <mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
                              <mo>+</mo>
                           </msup>
                           <mo linebreak="goodbreak">+</mo>
                           <mn>3</mn>
                           <msup>
                              <mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi>
                              <mo>−</mo>
                           </msup>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{\mathrm{Fe}} + {\mathrm{3N}}{{{\mathrm{a}}}_{\mathrm{2}}}{\mathrm{Se}} \leftrightarrow {\mathrm{N}}{{{\mathrm{a}}}_{\mathrm{3}}}{\mathrm{FeS}}{{{\mathrm{e}}}_{\mathrm{3}}} + {\mathrm{3N}}{{{\mathrm{a}}}^{\mathrm{ + }}} + {\mathrm{3}}{{{\mathrm{e}}}^ - }\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(4)</span></div>
         </div>
         
         <p>Benefiting from rational nanostructure, excellent sodium storage reversibility, and sensible defect concentration, the designed rod-like multi-cavity FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C nanocomposites are expected to have excellent performance in sodium-ion batteries. The cycling performance and coulombic efficiency (CE) of FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C, FeP/Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@C and FeP@C electrode materials at current density of 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> are shown in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0004">4a</a>. The FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C electrode has an initial discharge/charge capacity of 595.3/505.7&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, corresponding to a high initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) of 85% (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a>, Supporting Information). The high ICE presents a significant advantage compared to those reported in the literature (Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information). Moreover, the capacity of FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C still remains as high as 526.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles with an ultrahigh capacity retention of 88.4%. Wherein the carbon material contributes 30.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> capacity, as depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a> (Supporting Information). It is interesting that the capacity tends to decrease in the initial 20 cycles and then increases as the test cycles progress. This may be ascribed to the solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) film and by-products on the surface of the electrode material gradually stabilizing. Additionally, the pulverization of FePSe<sub>3</sub> nanoparticles during cycling results in more active sites for Na<sup>+</sup> storage, thereby leading to a continuous increment in capacity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404320-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404320-bib-0006_R_d137875623e1669" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Appl. Surf. Sci. J. Mater. Chem. A Chem. Eng. J.">6</a>, <a href="#adfm202404320-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404320-bib-0007_R_d137875623e1669" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Appl. Surf. Sci. J. Mater. Chem. A Adv. Funct. Mater.">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the FeP/Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@C and FeP@C electrode deliver a much lower capacity of 335.7 and 277.7&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles, corresponding to a low-capacity retention of 66% and 65%, respectively. Meanwhile, SEM images of the electrode materials revealed that the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C electrodes retained their intact rod morphology even after 100 cycles of complete sodication (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13a,b</a>, Supporting Information). In comparison, some of the rod morphology of the FeP@C electrode materials was preserved (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13e,f</a>, Supporting Information), albeit to a greater extent than the FeP/Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@C electrodes (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13c,d</a>, Supporting Information). It can be seen that FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C nanocomposite greatly outperformed FeP/Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@C and FeP@C anodes in terms of cycling stability and capacity, which can be attributed to the increase of active sites and sodium storage ability after the introduction of Se element. The FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C also displays the state-of-the art discharge capacities of 526.5, 464.3, 437.7, 398.5, 371.3, 344.5, and 329.3&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at various current densities of 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, and 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Especially, when the current density rises to 20&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C still delivers a large capacity of 321.7&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, which is 1.4 and 1.9 times higher than those of FeP/Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@C and FeP@C, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0004">4b</a>). Additionally, the capacity of the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C can be recovers to 500.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> as the rate switched back to the initial 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, suggesting the excellent structural stability. Moreover, as the current density increases, FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C electrode exhibits the most stable charge/discharge voltage profile and smallest voltage difference (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a>, Supporting Information), further indicating that the introduction of Se to the single-phase phosphide is advantageous for enhancing electrical conductivity and ionic diffusion capability. Meanwhile, in order to further demonstrate the outstanding sodium storage performance of FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C, the electrochemical performance of Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@C electrode had been tested, as depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a> (Supporting Information). The initial discharge capacity of the Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@C electrode was 580.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at current density of 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, with an ICE of 78%, significantly lower than that of the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C electrode (85%). The rate performance indicates that the Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@C electrode degrades more rapidly at higher current densities. Specifically, at 20&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, it demonstrates reversible capacity of only 239.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Additionally, at current density of 2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, rapid degradation occurs after ≈150 cycles. Subsequently, the capacity diminishes to only 55&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 500 cycles, likely attributed to the substantial volume change of the electrode material under high current conditions.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202404320-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/de91ff47-97e3-4742-859e-fbbc452d9272/adfm202404320-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/de91ff47-97e3-4742-859e-fbbc452d9272/adfm202404320-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/9d37d7ce-b309-4f8b-a753-c8c48ed38a38/adfm202404320-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/de91ff47-97e3-4742-859e-fbbc452d9272/adfm202404320-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202404320-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202404320" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Cycling stability at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and b) rate abilities at 0.1 to 20&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> of FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C, FeP/Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@C and FeP@C electrodes. c) Capacitive contribution at 0.8&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> of the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C electrode. In situ EIS profiles of the d) FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C and e) FeP@C electrodes recorded during the initial cycle at a current rate of 50&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. f) The evolution of R<sub>SEI</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> during cycling in FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C and FeP@C electrodes. g) Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients of FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C and FeP@C electrode at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after the 5th cycles. h) The performance and i) AFM images after long-term cycling of the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C, FeP/Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@C and FeP@C electrodes at 2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. j) The height plots of measuring distance corresponding to images of 2D AFM.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <div class="paragraph-element">To gain insights into the underlying mechanism behind the rapid Na<sup>+</sup> ion storage capacity of the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C electrode, a kinetic study was conducted based on the cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves obtained at various scan rates. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16a</a> (Supporting Information), as the scan rate gradually increased from 0.2 to 1.2&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, the CV curve of FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C maintained its well-defined shape, indicating minimal electrode polarization during the charging/discharging process. The relationship between peak current (i) and scan rate (v) can serve as a tool to discern whether the current is governed by a surface capacitance reaction or an ion diffusion reaction:<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404320-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404320-bib-0041_R_d137875623e1846" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Adv. Energy Mater. Adv. Energy Mater.">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>
            
            <div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202404320-disp-0005"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/a6ac6487-65e9-42fd-bc2a-e3bdfb50babc/adfm202404320-math-0005.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202404320:adfm202404320-math-0005" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202404320-math-0005.png">
                     <semantics>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">i</mi>
                           <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
                           <msup>
                              <mi mathvariant="normal">v</mi>
                              <mi mathvariant="normal">b</mi>
                           </msup>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation} {\mathrm{i}} = {\mathrm{a}} {{{\mathrm{v}}}^{\mathrm{b}}}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(5)</span></div>
            <div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202404320-disp-0006"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/aa0836fa-21ea-4e75-a97a-9b46fdb65e5f/adfm202404320-math-0006.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202404320:adfm202404320-math-0006" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202404320-math-0006.png">
                     <semantics>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi>logi</mi>
                           <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                           <mi>blogv</mi>
                           <mo linebreak="goodbreak">+</mo>
                           <mi>loga</mi>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{\mathrm{logi}} = {\mathrm{blogv}} + {\mathrm{loga}}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(6)</span></div>
         </div>
         
         <p>The b value can be utilized to analyze the associated electronic kinetics. Specifically, when the b value is close to 0.5, it indicates domination by the ionic diffusion process. Conversely, a b value approaching 1.0 signifies a surface pseudocapacitive behavior. The calculated b-values (0.822 to 0.996) for FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C electrode based on redox peak are higher than that of FeP@C electrode (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16b–d</a>, Supporting Information), suggests that the predominant influence on the Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism is the surface capacitance. Subsequently, we conducted detailed calculations using CV plots at various scan rates by relating (i  =  k<sub>1</sub> v  +  k<sub>2</sub>v<sup>1/2</sup>) to precisely discern the contribution attributed to Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion or double-layer capacitance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404320-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404320-bib-0003_R_d137875623e1904" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater.">3</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The k<sub>1</sub>v and k<sub>2</sub>v<sup>1/2</sup> represent non-Faraday and Faraday reactions, respectively. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0004">4c</a>, the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C electrode demonstrates a substantial capacitance contribution, reaching 85.1% higher than 72.4% of FeP@C at 0.8&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. Furthermore, the capacitive contribution of FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C increases from 79.5 to 89.3% as the scan rate rises from 0.2 to 1.2&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, which is significantly higher than that of the FeP@C at every scan rate (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a>, Supporting Information). These results indicate that Se-doped FeP@C is more conducive to promoting surface pseudocapacitive charge storage. To further illustrate the effect of Se doping on charge transport kinetics, in-situ electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) was performed on FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C and FeP@C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0004">4d,e</a>). The in situ EIS curves of the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C and FeP@C electrodes exhibit similarities, characterized by semicircles in the high-frequency region and diagonal lines in the low-frequency region. The concave semicircle in the electrochemical impedance spectra corresponds to the charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) and the SEI film resistance (R<sub>s</sub>). Meanwhile, the low-frequency diagonal line is associated with the Warburg impedance (Zw), representing Na<sup>+</sup> ion diffusion.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404320-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404320-bib-0042_R_d137875623e1946" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Small">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Upon fitting the EIS curves of the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C and FeP@C using the equivalent circuits (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18</a>, Supporting Information),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404320-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404320-bib-0006_R_d137875623e1957" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Appl. Surf. Sci. J. Mater. Chem. A Chem. Eng. J.">6</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> the results indicate that the values of <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> and R<sub>s</sub> in the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C are significantly smaller than those observed in FeP@C electrode (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0004">4f</a>). Moreover, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C in the initial state is very low, and it exhibits mild fluctuations during throughout the charging and discharging cycles in comparison to FeP@C. These observations suggest that the introduction of Se effectively increases the electrical conductivity and reduces interfacial resistance of the material, thereby improving rate performance. The galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) was used to further explore the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients (D<sub>Na+</sub>) during the sodiation-dediation process (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a>, Supporting Information). The calculation results show that the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C electrode distinguishes itself with a larger D<sub>Na+</sub> value compared to FeP@C in both sodiation and desodiation processes (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0004">4g</a>). This finding confirms the enhanced charge transfer and improved Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics achieved through the strategic Se substitution and the incorporation of a multicavity nanostructure.</p>
         
         <p>Considering the rapid kinetics and unique structure, the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C electrode was subjected to evaluation at high current densities of 2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> for extended periods. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0004">4h</a>, the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C electrode delivers a high discharge capacity of 338&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with 85% capacity retention after 1000 cycles, showcasing excellent cycling stability. In comparison, the capacity retention rate for FeP@C and FeP/Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@C were only 46% and 43% after 1000 cycles. Additionally, the corresponding atomic force microscopy (AFM) images indicate that FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C experiences least surface roughness change after 1000 cycles compared to FeP@C and FeP/Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0004">4i</a>). Moreover, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0004">4j</a> and Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20–S22</a> (Supporting Information), the volume expansion of FeP/Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@C and FeP@C increased by 100 and 70 times, respectively, compared to the pre-cycle period. In contrast, FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C experienced a much more modest expansion of only ≈20 times. From the above discussion, the doping of Se in a single transition metal phosphide, coupled with the creation of a distinctive multi-cavity structure, plays a crucial role in mitigating the volume expansion of the electrode material during cycling. Consequently, this improvement contributes to enhancing the stability and kinetic behavior of the electrode material. In comparison to previously reported SIBs anode materials with double anion doping, FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C exhibits overwhelming benefits in specific capacity and cycling stability (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404320-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404320-bib-0002_R_d137875623e2042" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Natl. Sci. Rev. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Small">2</a>, <a href="#adfm202404320-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404320-bib-0005_R_d137875623e2042" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Chem. Eng. J. Energy Storage Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater.">5</a>, <a href="#adfm202404320-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404320-bib-0013_R_d137875623e2042" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Adv. Mater.">13</a>, <a href="#adfm202404320-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404320-bib-0018_R_d137875623e2042" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater. Adv. Mater. Interfaces Adv. Funct. Mater.">18</a>, <a href="#adfm202404320-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404320-bib-0033_R_d137875623e2042" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Chem. Eng. J.">33</a>, <a href="#adfm202404320-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404320-bib-0043_R_d137875623e2042" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - J. Power Sources ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Adv. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Chem. Eng. J.">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Therefore, FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C electrode materials emerge as promising candidates for high-capacity and durable anode materials in sodium-ion batteries.</p>
         
         <p>To gain fundamental insights into the significantly enhanced electrochemical activity and stability of FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C, density functional theory (DFT) calculations were performed to explore the structural advantages of FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C compared to FeP@C and Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@C for Na<sup>+</sup> storage. <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0005">5a</a> shows the schematic diagram of differential charge after adsorption of Na on the surface of the sample, and the corresponding cross-sectional charge distribution. We can see that the adsorption of Na on the surface of FePSe<sub>3</sub> shows more charge transfer and is more favorable for the capture of Na<sup>+</sup>, which will be beneficial to improve the redox reaction activity. Meanwhile, the sodium ion adsorption process for FeP, FePSe<sub>3</sub> and Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub> was simulated, as illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24</a> (Supporting Information). The adsorption energy of FePSe<sub>3</sub> (−2.62&nbsp;eV) was found to be lower than that of FeP (−2.51&nbsp;eV) and Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub> (−2.56&nbsp;eV), indicating its stronger Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption capacity (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0005">5b</a>). Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0005">5c</a> shows the crystal orbital Hamilton population (COHP) analysis based on Fe-P bonding of FeP and Fe-Se bonding interactions in FePSe<sub>3</sub> and Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>. It can be found that the integrated COHP of FePSe<sub>3</sub> is lower than that of FeP and Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub> at the Fermi energy level, which implies easier fracture in the transformation reaction, faster reaction kinetics and higher reversibility. Subsequently, the diffusion behavior of Na<sup>+</sup> in various materials was examined. The simulation portraying the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion process across different materials, advancing from position 1 to position 5, is illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0005">5d,e</a> and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25</a> (Supporting Information). It's worth noting that the diffusion barrier of FePSe<sub>3</sub>, with the incorporation of Se atoms, is notably lower at 0.37&nbsp;eV compared to FeP (0.41&nbsp;eV) and Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub> (0.51&nbsp;eV), suggesting a more facile diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup> in FePSe<sub>3</sub>. (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0005">5f</a>). The relatively low diffusion energy barrier favours fast ion diffusion and electrochemical reaction kinetics. Meanwhile, the density of states (DOS) of FeP, FePSe<sub>3</sub> and Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub> is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0005">5g</a>, which shows that FePSe<sub>3</sub> has a higher density of states near the Fermi energy level and exhibits superior electronic conductivity. On the other hand, in order to better understand the solvation structure of NaPF<sub>6</sub> in different organic solvents, this work simulated the solvation structure of NaPF<sub>6</sub> in two electrolytes with machine learning potentials. The solvation energies of Na<sup>+</sup> in two different organic solvents of diethylene glycol dimethyl ether (DIGLYEM) and ethylene carbonate (EC), diethyl carbonate (DEC), and methyl ethyl carbonate (EMC) composite were calculated as shown in detail in Supporting Information. A schematic model of NaPF<sub>6</sub> in solvents EC_DEC_EMC (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0005">5h</a>) and DIGLYME (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0005">5i</a>) was generated through machine learning. Subsequently, solvation energies were computed following molecular dynamics simulations. Notably, the solvation energy value in DIGLYEM is higher, measuring at −5.32&nbsp;eV. This higher value indicates a lower desolvation energy, consequently enhancing the kinetics of the desolvation step.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404320-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404320-bib-0044_R_d137875623e2163" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater.">44</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Meanwhile, the radial distribution functions of the two electrolytes are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0005">5j</a>, where both Na-ODIGLYME and Na-OEC_DEC_EMC are predominantly distributed ≈2.3&nbsp;Å, indicating that they are mainly distributed in the first solvated shell layer. Compared with Na-FEC_DEC_EMC, Na-FDIGLYME is concentrated in smaller distances, indicating stronger Na-F interactions between Na<sup>+</sup> and PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup>, which facilitates the formation of dense fluorine-rich solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) films on the electrode surface.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404320-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404320-bib-0045_R_d137875623e2177" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - ACS Energy Lett.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> These findings are further supported experimentally when using ester electrolyte. An analysis of the differential charge versus voltage curves of the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C electrode over multiple cycles demonstrates a diminishing and eventual disappearance of the peak at 1.8&nbsp;V as the number of cycles increases (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26a,b</a>, Supporting Information). In contrast, when employing an ether electrolyte, nearly overlapping curves are observed. This observation confirms the stability and reversibility of the sodiumation/desodiumation reaction during the cycling process. Moreover, under the influence of the ester electrolyte, the specific capacity of the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C electrode experiences a rapid decline, essentially approaching zero after 500 cycles at a current density of 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26c</a>, Supporting Information). However, a high capacity of 439&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 500 cycles can be achieved in the ether electrolyte, highlighting the superior suitability of the low de-solvation energy.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202404320-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/ae352174-5fea-4fbf-a775-41ed46c0a758/adfm202404320-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/ae352174-5fea-4fbf-a775-41ed46c0a758/adfm202404320-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/d9caf9a0-87c0-41c1-b6e9-c21f714514c0/adfm202404320-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/ae352174-5fea-4fbf-a775-41ed46c0a758/adfm202404320-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202404320-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202404320" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) The charge density difference of Na adsorption, and the cross-sectional charge distribution, b) Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption energy of FeP, FePSe<sub>3</sub>, Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>. c) the COHP and ICOHP in the FeP, FePSe<sub>3</sub>, Fe<sub>3</sub>Se. d,e) Schematic diagram of simulated diffusion paths of Na<sup>+</sup> in different materials. f) Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion energy barrier of FeP, FePSe<sub>3</sub>, Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>. g) The total density of states. h,i) Schematic of the model and solvation energy of Na<sup>+</sup> in EC_DEC_EMC and DIGLYME solvents. j) Radial distribution functions g(r) of Na–O and Na–F pairs in both electrolytes.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The results presented above clearly demonstrate that the single-phase ternary FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C nanoparticles embedded in an MOF-derived multicavity carbon matrix possess multiple advantages for Na<sup>+</sup> ion storage: i) the presence of a unique multi-cavity structure and a large specific surface area not only facilitates ample electrolyte ion infiltration but also mitigates volume expansion during cycling, resulting in good cycle stability; ii) the introduction of Se atom doping influences the electronic structure of the central metal Fe atom, enlarges ion diffusion channels and reduces diffusion energy barriers, thereby accelerating the fast redox reaction kinetics; iii) the abundant anionic defects creates numerous new reaction active sites and enhances the intrinsic electrical conductivity, contributing to a remarkable pseudo-capacitance storage. Consequently, the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C electrode demonstrates the optimal electrochemical performance for SIBs.</p>
         
         <p>Additionally, a sodium-ion full cell was assembled using FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C anode and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>@C (NVP@C) cathode to assess the overall performance of the full cell device, which schematic diagram is illustrated in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0006">6a</a>. The electrochemical properties of NVP@C and the morphological characterization are detailed in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27</a> (Supporting Information). In Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0006">6b</a>, charge/discharge curves of voltage versus normalized capacity are plotted using the NVP@C cathode, FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C anode, and full cell voltage. The output voltage of the full cell is observed to display a cathode-anode voltage difference. Furthermore, the integral calculation results in an operating voltage of 2.65&nbsp;V during discharge. The NVP@C//FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C full cell exhibits an initial reversible capacity of 81.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at current density of 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0006">6c</a>). The charge/discharge curves across the first three cycles demonstrate excellent overlap, achieving a coulombic efficiency close to 100%. The cycling performance is further illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0006">6d</a>, revealing a remaining reversible capacity of 78&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles, with a capacity retention of 96%. The charge and discharge curves for different cycles are displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28</a> (Supporting Information). For comparison, sodium ion full cells were also assembled using FeP/Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@C and FeP@C anodes with NVP@C, and their electrochemical performance was tested. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S29a</a> (Supporting Information), NVP@C//FeP/Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@C at a current density of 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> exhibited a capacity of only 68.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles, while NVP@C//FeP@C demonstrated a noticeable decay trend during cycling. Moreover, a series of light-emitting diodes (LEDs) are successfully illuminated using an NVP@C//FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C button cell (inset in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0006">6d</a>), thus emphasizing the potential application of the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C anode in SIBs. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0006">6e</a> illustrates the full-cell rate performance, demonstrating high-capacity retention even at current densities ranging from 0.1 to 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Furthermore, ≈100.0% of reversible capacity (86 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) can be recovered as the rate switched return to 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Compared to the main sample, the capacity of NVP@C//FeP/Fe<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@C decays more rapidly with increasing current density (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S29b</a>, Supporting Information). The NVP@C//FeP@C demonstrates relative stability but exhibits a lower capacity, reaching only 52&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> when the current density returns to 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. The calculated energy and power densities of the NVP@C//FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C full cell is illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404320-fig-0006">6f</a>. In this configuration, the full cell delivers a maximum energy density of 202&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> at a power density of 225&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> and maintains a good energy density of 86&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> even at an ultra-high current density of 3480&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>, surpassing many state-of-the-art sodium-ion full batteries reported in previous literature.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404320-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404320-bib-0046_R_d137875623e2359" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Nano Energy J. Mater. Chem. A Adv. Mater. ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng. J. Mater. Chem. A Adv. Sci. Nano-Micro Lett.">46</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202404320-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/4205a2c1-2967-416f-a930-4d4ecc57d29f/adfm202404320-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/4205a2c1-2967-416f-a930-4d4ecc57d29f/adfm202404320-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/97df670a-dc43-485d-ba48-c7670e9d3f9e/adfm202404320-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/4205a2c1-2967-416f-a930-4d4ecc57d29f/adfm202404320-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202404320-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202404320" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Schematic illustration of the sodium-ion full cell with Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>@C//FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C couple. b) Normalised charge/discharge curves, c) charge/discharge curves and d) cycling stability at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Inset of photograph of LED lights powered by the full cell), e) rate performance. f) Ragone plots of the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>@C//FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C device compared with previously reported SIBs full cell.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202404320-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202404320-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusions</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, we have developed a facile method to synthesize rod-like multicavity FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C nanocomposites. The rod-like multicavity structure provides a fast electron diffusion path and accommodates the volume expansion during cycling. The systematically experimentally investigated and DFT calculation demonstrate that the introduction of Se is not only beneficial for abundant reaction sites and improved intrinsic electronic conductivity but also increases the adsorption energy and reduces the diffusion energy barrier for Na<sup>+</sup>, thus accelerating the redox reaction kinetics and enhancing the reversibility of the transformation/alloying reaction. Moreover, the physical phase transformation mechanism of FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C during the sodiation/desodiation process was investigated by combining in-situ XRD, ex situ TEM and XPS. Thanks to the unique multi-cavity structure and physical phase composition, the FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C electrode exhibits high reversible capacity, excellent rate performance (321.7&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 20&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), and good long-cycle performance. Additionally, it was assembled with Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>@C to form NVP@C//FePSe<sub>3</sub>@C sodium-ion full batteries, which exhibited energy densities up to 202&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>. This work effectively addresses the challenges associated with the fast-charging anode materials for SIBs, offering a new insight for developing high-performance materials for battery systems.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
